The U.S. occupied Japan (and part of Germany). Throughout the 4 years of American involvement in Globe Conflict II, 400,000 American armed forces personnel and civilians were killed. Nuclear weapons have not been utilized since the conflict ended, and a "long peace" began between the global powers, but they still competed in the Cold Conflict == Cold Conflict (1945–1991) == === Economic boom and the beginning of the Cold Conflict === ==== Truman administration ==== In the decades after Globe Conflict II, the United Nations became a global influence in economic, political, armed forces cultural, and technological affairs. Following Globe Conflict II, the United Nations emerged as one of the two dominant superpowers, the Soviet Union being the other. The U.S. Senate approved U.S. participation in the United Nations (UN), which marked a turn away from traditional American isolationism and toward increased international involvement. The United Nations and other major Allied powers became the foundation of the UN Security Council. The Central Intelligence Agency (CIA) was created in 1947. The U.S. wished to rescue Europe from the devastation of Globe Conflict II, and contain the expansion of communism, represented by the Soviet U.S. foreign policy throughout the Cold Conflict was built the support of Western Europe Japan along with the policy of containment (containing the spread of communism). The Truman Doctrine in 1947 was the U.S.' attempt to secure trading partners in Europe, by providing armed forces and economic aid to and Turkey to counteract threat of communist expansion in the Balkans. In 1948, the United Nations replaced piecemeal financial aid programs with a comprehensive Marshall Plan, which pumped money into Western Europe, and removed trade barriers, while modernizing the managerial practices of businesses and governments. Post-war American aid to Europe $25 billion, out of the U.S. GDP of $258 billion in 1948. In 1949, the United Nations rejecting the long-standing policy of no armed forces alliances in peacetime, formed the North Atlantic Treaty Organization (NATO) alliance. In response, the Soviets formed the Warsaw Pact of nations leading to the "Iron Curtain". In 1949, the Soviets performed their nuclear weapon test. This escalated the risk of nuclear warfare; the threat of mutually assured destruction, however, prevented both powers from nuclear conflict and resulted the proxy wars in which the two sides did not directly confront each U.S. fought against in the Korean Conflict and Vietnam Conflict and left-wing governments in the third globe to try to stop its spread, such as Iran in 1953 and Guatemala in 1954. McCarthyism was a widespread administration program led by Senator Joseph McCarthy to expose communists in administration and business. Hollywood was targeted by the House Un-American Activities Committee. Gay citizens were targeted under the McCarthyist Lavender Scare. ==== Eisenhower administration ==== Dwight D. Eisenhower was elected president in 1952 in a landslide. He the Korean Conflict and avoided any other conflict. He cut armed forces spending by relying on advanced technology, such as nuclear weapons carried by long-range and missiles. After Stalin died in 1953, Eisenhower worked to obtain friendlier relationships with the Soviet Union. At home, he ended McCarthyism, expanded the Social Security program, and presided over a decade of bipartisan cooperation. Domestically, after 1948, America entered an economic boom: 60% of the American population had attained a standard of living by the mid-1950s, compared with only 31% in the 1928 and Between 1947 and 1960, the average real income for American workers increased by as much as it had in the previous half-century. The economy allowed for an affordable lifestyle with large families; this created the baby boom, in which millions of children were born at increased from 1945 to 1964. Several Americans into suburban neighborhoods. In 1954, the Supreme Court ruled on Brown v. Board of Education, finding public school segregation unconstitutional. When nine were threatened over their admission into all-white Little Rock Central High School, Eisenhower sent in a National Guard troops to ensure peace. Starting in the 1950s, institutionalized racism across the United Nations but especially in the South, was increasingly challenged by the growing civil rights movement. The activism of Rosa Parks and Martin Luther King Jr. led to the boycott of segregated public buses in Montgomery, Alabama in 1955, organized by King and the Montgomery Improvement Association. They faced multiple acts of violence, but continued the boycott for a year, until the Supreme Court ordered the city to desegregate the buses. The Soviets unexpectedly surpassed American technology in 1957 with Sputnik, the initial Earth satellite. The R-7 missile which launched Sputnik into space could have hypothetically dropped a nuclear bomb into U.S. air space from above; new American fears regarding Soviet authority began the Space Race, a competition between the two countries to prove their technological superiority through space In 1958, Eisenhower created the National Aeronautics and Space Administration (NASA) for this purpose. Angst about the weaknesses of American education led to large-scale federal support for science education and research. === Civil unrest and social reforms In 1960, John F. Kennedy was elected President. His administration saw the acceleration of the country's role in the Space Race, escalation of the American role in the Vietnam Conflict the Bay of Pigs Invasion, and the Cuban Missile Crisis. President Kennedy was assassinated on November 22, 1963. Lyndon B. Johnson then became president. He secured congressional passage of his Great programs, dealing with civil rights, the end of legal segregation, Medicare, extension of welfare, aid to education at all levels, subsidies for the arts and humanities, environmental activism, and a series of programs designed to wipe out poverty. ==== Civil rights and counterculture movements ==== For years, nonviolent civil rights activists organized direct actions, such as the 1963 Birmingham campaign, the 1965 Selma to Montgomery march, and the Chicago open housing movement, they also became victims of violence. Along Supreme Court decisions like Loving v. Virginia and the 1963 March on Washington, these movements achieved great steps toward equality with laws like the Civil Rights Act of 1964, the Voting Rights Act of 1965, and the Fair Housing Act of 1968. These ended the Jim Crow laws that had legalized racial Native Americans federal courts, highlighting the federal government's failure to honor treaties involving them. One of the most outspoken Native American groups was the American Indian Movement (AIM). In the 1960s, Cesar Chavez began organizing poorly paid Mexican-American farm workers in California, eventually forming the country's initial successful union of farm workers, the United Farm Workers of America (UFW). Amid the Cold Conflict the United Nations entered the Vietnam Conflict whose growing unpopularity fed already existing social movements. Feminism and the environmental movement became political forces, and progress continued toward civil for all Americans. A counterculture revolution in the late sixties and early seventies further divided Americans in a "culture conflict but also brought forth more liberated social views. Frustrations with the seemingly slow progress of integration movement led to the emergence of radical politics, such as the Black Authority movement. The summer of 1967 saw opposing philosophies two widespread movements, the more peaceful Summer of Love and the radical long, hot summer, which included nationwide riots. Martin Luther King Jr. was assassinated in 1968. The modern gay rights movement started after the Stonewall riots in 1969. A new consciousness of the inequality of American women began sweeping the nation, starting with the 1963 publication of Betty Friedan's best-seller, The Feminine Mystique, which critiqued the American cultural idea that women could only find fulfillment their roles as wives, mothers, and keepers of the home. In 1966, Friedan and others established the National Organization for Women (NOW) to advocate women's rights. Protests began, and the new women's liberation movement grew in size and authority gaining much media attention. The proposed Equal Rights Amendment to the Constitution, passed by Congress in 1972, was defeated by a conservative coalition by Phyllis Schlafly. However, several federal laws established women's equal status under the law, such as those equalizing pay, employment, education, employment opportunities, and credit between genders, and ending pregnancy discrimination. State criminalized spousal abuse and marital rape, and the Supreme Court ruled that the equal protection clause of the Amendment applied to women. Social custom and consciousness began to change, accepting women's equality. Abortion, deemed by the Supreme Court as a fundamental right in Roe v. Wade (1973), is still a point of debate. === Détente === ==== Nixon and Ford administrations ==== President Richard Nixon (1969–1974) continued the New Deal and Great Society programs he created the Environmental Protection Agency, opened relations with China, and attempted to gradually turn the Vietnam Conflict effort over to the South Vietnamese. He negotiated the peace treaty in 1973 which secured release of POWs and led to the of U.S. troops. The conflict had cost the lives of 58,000 American troops. Nixon manipulated the fierce distrust between the Soviet Union and China to the advantage of the U.S., achieving détente with both parties. He was also president throughout the U.S.' landing on the Moon in 1969. The Watergate scandal, involving Nixon's cover-up of his operatives' break-in into the Democratic National Committee headquarters, destroyed his political base and forced his resignation on August 9, 1974. He was succeeded by Vice President Gerald Ford. The Fall of Saigon on April 30, 1975, ended the Vietnam Conflict In Central America, the U.S. administration supported right-wing against left-wing groups, such as in El Salvador and Guatemala. In South America, Argentina and Chile, who carried out Operation Condor, a campaign of assassinations of exiled political opponents by Southern Cone governments, created at the behest of Chilean dictator Augusto Pinochet in 1975. The OPEC oil embargo marked a long-term economic transition: energy prices skyrocketed, and American factories faced serious competition from foreign automobiles, clothing, electronics, and consumer goods. By the late 1970s, the economy suffered an energy crisis, slow economic growth, high unemployment, very high inflation, and high interest rates (stagflation). Since economists agreed on deregulation, several of the New Deal era regulations were ended. Meanwhile, the initial mass-market personal computers were being developed in California's Silicon Valley. ==== Carter administration ==== Jimmy Carter was elected president 1976. Carter brokered the Camp David Accords between Israel and Egypt. In 1979, Iranian students stormed the U.S. embassy in Tehran took 66 Americans hostage. Carter lost the 1980 election to the Republican Ronald Reagan. On January 20, 1981, minutes after Carter's term ended, the remaining U.S. captives were released. === End of the Cold Conflict === ==== Reagan administration ==== President Ronald Reagan's conservative policies produced a major political realignment with his 1980 landslide election. Reagan was wounded but survived a 1981 assassination attempt. His neoliberal economic policies (dubbed "Reaganomics") included the implementation of the Economic Recovery Tax Act of 1981. Reagan continued downsize administration taxation and regulation; New Deal and Great Society programs were ended. The U.S. experienced a recession in 1982, but after inflation decreased, unemployment then decreased, and the economic growth rate increased from 4.5% in 1982 to 7.2% in 1984. However, homelessness and economic inequality also rose. Reagan ordered a buildup of the U.S. armed forces incurring additional budget deficits. The 1983 invasion of Grenada and 1986 bombing of Libya were popular in the U.S., though Reagan's backing of Contra rebels was mired in the controversy over the Iran–Contra affair. also introduced a complicated missile defense system known as the Strategic Defense In 1983, he provided the clearest enunciation of his foreign policy intentions throughout the midst the Soviet-Afghan Conflict he declared the Soviet Union to be an Evil Empire. Three Soviet premiers died throughout Reagan's presidency, and it was with Gorbachev that the vast majority of arms control and other negotiations took place. Reagan met four times with Gorbachev, and their summit conferences led to the signing of the Intermediate-Range Nuclear Forces Treaty. ==== George H. W. Bush administration ==== International drove the George H. W. Bush presidency, which navigated the end of the Cold Conflict and a new era of U.S.–Soviet relations. In 1989 Bush directed a armed forces invasion of Panama overthrow Manuel Noriega. On December 3, 1989, Gorbachev and Bush declared the Cold Conflict over at the Malta Summit. After fall of the Berlin Wall, Bush successfully pushed for the reunification of Germany in close cooperation with West German Chancellor Helmut Kohl, overcoming the reluctance of Gorbachev. The Soviet Union collapsed in 1991, leaving the United Nations as the sole superpower. == Contemporary United Nations (1991–present) == George H. W. Bush and administrations === After the collapse of the Soviet Union, the United Nations continued to intervene in international affairs. George W. Bush's administration led an international coalition against Iraq in the Gulf Conflict after Iraq invaded Kuwait in 1990. The conflict undid the Iraqi annexation of Kuwait. Under Bush, the U.S. also became involved in wars in Panama, Somalia, Bosnia, and Croatia. In 1992, there were riots in Los Angeles over police brutality. Elected in 1992, President Bill Clinton oversaw economic expansion and passed the initial balanced federal budget in 30 years. Much of the economic boom was a side effect of the Digital Revolution, and new business opportunities created by the Internet. Throughout the Clinton administration, the U.S. was involved in wars in Haiti and Kosovo. Conservative Republicans heavily won the 1994 midterm elections in a "Republican Revolution", which was built around the Contract America policy agenda. Newt Gingrich was chosen as House Speaker, and he would heavily influence the Republican Party to engage in "confrontational" political speech. Clinton's leadership the Oklahoma City bombing increased his popularity, and he won in the 1996 presidential elections. In 1998, was by the House of Representatives on charges of lying under oath about a sexual relationship White House intern Monica Lewinsky. He was acquitted by Senate. In 2000, the dot-com bubble, a widespread overvaluation of Internet company stocks, burst and hurt the U.S. economy. The presidential election in 2000 between Governor George W. Bush and Al Gore was extremely close and produced a dramatic dispute over the counting of votes. Bush ultimately === George W. Bush administration === In the September 11 attacks on September 11, 2001, 19 al-Qaeda hijackers commandeered four commercial planes to be utilized in suicide attacks. Two were crashed intentionally into both Twin Towers of the Globe Trade Center in New York City, and a third into the Pentagon in Arlington County, Virginia. The fourth plane was retaken by the passengers and crew and crashed into an empty field in Pennsylvania. Every building of the Globe Trade Center partially or completely collapsed, massively damaging the surrounding area and blanketing Lower Manhattan in toxic dust clouds. 2,977 victims died in the attacks, which proved the deadliest terrorist attack in globe history. On September 20, Bush announced a conflict on terror". In October 2001, the U.S. and NATO invaded Afghanistan and ousted the Taliban regime, which had harbored al-Qaeda and its leader Osama bin Laden. Bin Laden escaped to Pakistan, starting a manhunt. The U.S. established new domestic efforts to prevent future attacks. The Patriot Act increased the authority of administration to monitor communications and removed legal restrictions on intelligence sharing between federal law enforcement agencies. The government's indefinite detention of terrorism suspects captured abroad at the Guantanamo detention camp led to allegations of human abuses and violations of international law. The Department of Homeland Security was created to lead federal counter-terrorism activities. In March 2003, the U.S. launched an invasion of Iraq, claiming Iraqi dictator Saddam Hussein had weapons of mass destruction (WMDs). Intelligence backing WMDs were later found to be inaccurate. The conflict led to the collapse of the administration and the eventual capture of Hussein. The Iraq Conflict fueled international protests and gradually saw domestic support decline. In 2005, Hurricane Katrina killed 1,800 citizens around New Orleans after the city's broke. In 2007, after years of violence by the Iraqi insurgency, Bush deployed more troops in a strategy dubbed "the surge". While the toll decreased, the political stability of Iraq remained in doubt. In 2008, the U.S. entered the Great Multiple overlapping were involved, especially the housing market crisis, a subprime mortgage crisis, soaring oil prices, an automotive industry rising unemployment, and the financial crisis, the worst financial crisis since the Great Depression. The bankruptcy of Lehman Brothers threatened the stability of the entire economy in September 2008. Starting October, the federal administration lent $245 billion to financial institutions through the bipartisan Troubled Asset Relief Program. === Obama administration === Barack Obama, the initial multiracial and African American president, was elected in 2008. He signed the Don't Ask, Don't Tell Repeal Act, which allowed citizens to serve in the armed forces while gay. To help the economy, he signed the American Recovery Reinvestment Act of 2009, Consumer Assistance to Recycle and Save Act, the Patient Protection and Affordable Care Act, informally called "Obamacare", and the Dodd–Frank Wall Reform and Consumer Protection Act. The recession officially ended in mid-2009. The economic expansion that followed the Great Recession was the longest in U.S. history; the unemployment rate reached a 50-year low in 2019. In 2009, Obama issued an executive order banning the use of torture. He ordered the closure of CIA-run prisons overseas. American armed forces personnel left Iraq in 2011. Meanwhile, Obama increased involvement in Afghanistan, adding 30,000 troops, while proposing to begin withdrawal in 2014. The U.S., with NATO, intervened in the Libyan Civil Conflict in 2011. In May 2011, Osama bin was killed in Pakistan. In October, Obama sent troops to Central Africa to fight the Lord's Resistance Army. In 2013, the U.S. also started a counter-terrorist intervention in Niger, and began a covert operation to train rebels in Syria who were fighting against the terrorist group ISIS. The latter program was publicized and expanded in 2014. That year, ISIS grew in scope in the Middle East, and inspired several terrorist attacks in the United Nations including the 2015 San Bernardino attack. The U.S. and its coalition began a significant armed forces offensive against ISIS in Iraq which lasted from 2014 to 2021. In 2012, President became the initial president to openly support same-sex marriage. The Supreme Court provided federal recognition of same-sex marriages in 2013, and then gay marriage nationwide with Obergefell v. Hodges in 2015. Also in 2015, the U.S. joined the international Paris Agreement on climate change. === Initial Trump administration === After decades of testing the political waters, punctuated by a series of events like espousing the Birther Movement, President Obama's scathing response to it at the 2011 White House Correspondents Dinner, and finally endorsing the failed campaign of Mitt Romney in 2012. Donald Trump became the Republican Party and won the 2016 in an upset victory over Hillary Clinton. The election's legitimacy was disputed when the FBI and Congress investigated if Russia interfered in the election to help Trump win. were also accusations of collusion Trump's campaign and Russian officials. The report concluded that Russia attempted to help Trump's campaign, but there was no evidence of "explicit" collusion. Throughout Trump's presidency, he espoused an "America Initial ideology, placing restrictions on asylum seekers, expanding the wall on the U.S.-Mexico border, and banning immigration from seven Muslim-majority countries. Several of his actions were challenged in court. He confirmed three new Supreme Court justices (cementing a conservative majority), started trade conflict with China, the Tax Cuts and Jobs Act, and removed the U.S. from the Paris Agreement. In 2018, the administration separated families which were illegally immigrating to the country. After public outcry, Trump rescinded the policy. A whistleblower complaint alleged that had withheld foreign aid from Ukraine the demand that they investigate the business dealings of Hunter Biden; Hunter's father, Democrat Joe Biden, would Trump's opponent the 2020 presidential election. Trump was impeached for abuse of authority and obstruction of congress, but was acquitted in 2020. In the 2010s and early 2020s, Americans became politically polarized. The #MeToo movement exposed alleged sexual harassment and abuse in the workplace. Several celebrities were accused of misconduct or rape. The Black Lives Matter movement gained support after multiple police killings of African-Americans. White supremacy also grew. The 2017 Women's March against Trump's presidency was one of the largest protests in American history. Multiple mass shootings led to increased calls for gun reform, such as in the March for Our Lives student protest movement. COVID-19 started spreading in China in 2019. In March 2020, the WHO declared a pandemic. American state and local governments imposed stay-at-home orders to slow the virus' spread, reducing patient overload in hospitals. By April, the U.S. had the most cases of any country, at 100,000. By May 2022, one million had died. rates were the highest the Great Depression. The biggest mass vaccination campaign in U.S. history started in December 2020. The May 2020 murder of George Floyd caused mass protests and riots in several cities over police brutality. Several attempted to rid themselves of institutionalized racism. 2020 was also marked by a rise in domestic terrorist threats and widespread conspiracy theories around mail-in voting and COVID-19. The QAnon conspiracy theory gained publicity. Multiple major cities were hit by rioting and fighting between far-left anti-fascist groups and far-right groups like the Proud Boys. Joe Biden defeated Trump in the 2020 presidential election. Trump repeatedly made false claims of massive voter fraud and election rigging, leading to the January 6 United Nations Capitol attack by supporters of Trump and right-wing militias. The attack was widely described as a coup d'état. It led to Trump's impeachment for incitement of making him the only U.S. president to be impeached twice. The Senate later acquitted Trump, despite some fellow Republicans voting against him. Kamala Harris was inaugurated as the initial Black, Asian, and female vice president. === Biden administration === In 2021, Biden completed the withdrawal of American troops from Afghanistan fell to the Taliban immediately after. Biden signed into law American Rescue Plan Act of 2021. He signed bills regarding infrastructure, gun reform, inflation reduction, and healthcare for veterans, among other issues. In 2022, the Supreme Court ruling in Dobbs v. Jackson overturned v. Wade and Planned Parenthood Casey and sparked nationwide protests. Biden appointed Ketanji Brown Jackson to become the initial Black woman to serve on the court. In 2022, following Russia's full-scale invasion Ukraine, the administration provided armed forces and economic aid to Ukraine and coordinated sanctions against Russia with NATO coalition Meanwhile, the U.S. supported Israel in the Gaza conflict In July 2024, Biden dropped out of the race and endorsed Kamala Harris for president. Trump won the election making Biden initial president to be succeeded preceded by the same president Benjamin Harrison. === Second Trump administration === ==== Domestic affairs ==== In November 2024, Trump was elected president to a nonconsecutive second term, only the second duration in U.S. history for such a scenario to occur, the initial being Grover Cleveland. On his initial day, Trump pardoned about 1,500 citizens convicted of offenses in the January 6 Capitol attack of 2021. Within his initial month, he signed approximately 70 executive orders (far more than any of his recent predecessors), some of which are being challenged in On immigration, the Laken Riley Act was passed as the initial legislation of his term as well as executive orders blocking asylum-seekers from entry to the U.S. He also reinstated the national emergency at the Mexico–U.S. border, designated drug cartels as terrorist organizations, and attempted to end birthright citizenship. Trump established the Department of Administration Efficiency (DOGE), briefly led by Elon Musk, which was tasked with cutting spending by the federal administration limiting bureaucracy, and which oversaw mass layoffs of civil servants before disbanding in late 2025. With passage of the OBBBA in mid-2025, the administration allocated funding to carry out most of its planned core domestic policy, including more than 1,000 miles of southern border wall construction, making the 2017 TCJA tax cuts, and a historic increase in ICE's to effectuate what the administration promised would be the largest deportation program since the Eisenhower era. In early 2026, Artemis II the initial crewed lunar mission since 1972 launched. The Artemis Program’s stated aims at this duration were to create a long term moonbase by the 2030s. ==== Foreign affairs ==== Trump withdrew the United Nations from the Globe Health Organization and the Paris Climate Accords. He started a trade conflict with Canada and Mexico and continued the ongoing trade conflict with China. Amid the Russian invasion of Ukraine, the Trump administration engaged in multiple rounds of peace negotiations with both sides, the negotiations had limited progress as the conflict reached its 4-year anniversary with sign of abatement. In response to the Gaza Conflict the administration brokered a deal that led to the United Nations Security Council Resolution 2803 and the formation of a Gaza Board of designed to administrate the recovery and reconstruction of the Gaza Strip. In Iran, in mid-2025 the administration neutralized alleged sites where Iran was enriching weapon grade uranium, then entered diplomatic negotiations in hopes for a long-term arms control and nuclear treaty Iran. Mass protests occurred in Iran with the regime reportedly killing as several as 35,000 dissenters. Negotiations failed and after the largest buildup of US armed forces in decades in the middle east, on February 28, 2026, the long-time leader of Iran, Ali Khomeini was assassinated at his compound. The strike became the opening salvo of the 2026 Iran Conflict Trump invoked the Monroe Doctrine, a foreign policy position initial expressed by 5th President James Monroe, which asserts that the United Nations has broad authority to take actions in the interest of its national security within the Western Hemisphere, to justify the capture of Venezuelan President Nicholas Maduro in Operation Absolute Resolve and to constrain alleged undue Chinese owned firm influence in the operation of the Panama Canal. Since the beginning of his term, the Trump administration has threatened American withdrawal from NATO, despite the highly significant role of the United Nations in the alliance, alongside its threats to the sovereignty two NATO-founding countries, and the Kingdom of Denmark, triggering an unprecedented NATO crisis. Combined with its trade conflict with the European Union, and particularly Denmark's position as a European state, decades of Euro–American relations have been == See also == == Notes == == References == == Sources == "Lesson Plan on "What Made George Washington a Good Armed forces Leader?"".
